                return gptText.replace(/\^|\*|#|\$|\"|\'|\=|\,|\!|\+|\~|\;|\(|\)|\<|\>|\[|\]|\?|\%|\:|\@|\;|\&|\||\{|\}|\\|/g, '');
            }
            return "blank";
        }

            .setTargeting('property', 'value-of-property')    // Change and duplicate this line for as many additional keywords to send
            .setTargeting('doi', gptClean('10.1002/adfm.202406827')) // Publication DOI
            .setTargeting('pbPage', gptClean(gptPage))
            .setTargeting('pbSubPage', gptClean(gptSubPage))
            .setTargeting('urlpath', gptClean(document.location.pathname));

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="246c13580cb147ecb23c3c24f6cdfc44"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="246c13580cb147ecb23c3c24f6cdfc44">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '9309e124-69d4-4ed2-a641-400599ccdfef'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        (function() {
            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {
                var store_domain = 'https://advanced.onlinelibrary.wiley.com';
                var session_id = '72441F77F90EB9FEB1C884E51C674B6E';
                var url = ('https:' == document.location.protocol ? 'https://' : 'http://')
                    + "beacon.riskified.com?shop=" + store_domain + "&sid=" + session_id;
                var s = document.createElement('script');
                s.type = 'text/javascript';
                s.async = true;
                s.src = url;
                var x = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
                x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
            }
            if (window.attachEvent)
                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else
                window.addEventListener('load', riskifiedBeaconLoad, false);
        })();

                     <p>E-mail: <a class="corr-email" title="Link to email address" href="mailto:cwzhang@hebut.edu.cn"><span>cwzhang@hebut.edu.cn</span></a>; <a class="corr-email" title="Link to email address" href="mailto:wang.gongkai@hebut.edu.cn"><span>wang.gongkai@hebut.edu.cn</span></a></p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Zhang/Chengwei">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Gou/Huiyang" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a7" data-db-target-for="a7" aria-controls="a7" aria-haspopup="true" id="a7_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Huiyang Gou</span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a7" aria-labelledby="a7_Ctrl" role="region" id="a7">
                     <p class="author-name">Huiyang Gou</p>
                     <p>Center for High Pressure Science and Technology Advanced Research, Beijing, 100094 China</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Gou/Huiyang">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Wang/Gongkai" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a8" data-db-target-for="a8" aria-controls="a8" aria-haspopup="true" id="a8_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Gongkai Wang<i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-mail_outline"></i></span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a8" aria-labelledby="a8_Ctrl" role="region" id="a8">

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d411807880" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>The rise of Na-storage devices has put forward higher requirements for Na-storage anode materials with large capacity, long service life, and fast rate capability. Mesoporous carbons, either as active materials or as hosts for guest active nanoparticles, are considered as promising electrode materials. However, addressing the issues of their short lifespan resulting from volume variation and the low coulombic efficiency caused by large surface area via a facile porous structure design still remains a challenge. Herein, a versatile phosphorus-doped mesoporous carbon (PMC) armed is developed by graphene aerogel (GA) (GA@PMC) for hosting Na-storage active nanoparticles. As a case study, FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles are selectively supported onto this GA@PMC matrix, creating the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC composite.&nbsp;When employed in typical Na-storage devices, such as Na-ion batteries, Na-ion hybrid capacitors, and Na-ion based dual-ion batteries, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC electrode consistently demonstrates superior electrochemical performance. In such GA@PMC, the conformal GA can improve the entire conductivity while decreasing the specific surface area that is directly contacting with electrolyte. The interconnected macroporous structure can not only promote the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> but also buffers the volume change of the guest active nanoparticles. This bespoke carbon platform synergistically endows the electrode material with enhanced rate capability, cyclic stability, and coulombic efficiency, which are being expected in advanced Na-storage devices.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406827-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406827-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Various newly developed energy storage systems, including sodium (Na)-ion based storage devices (SSDs) of Na-ion batteries (SIBs), Na-ion hybrid capacitors (SICs), and Na-based dual-ion batteries (SDIBs) have attracted considerable attention in recent decades as alternatives to Li-ion batteries for applications in electric vehicles, portable electronic devices or smart grids.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0001_R_d411807872e433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Adv. Energy Mater.">1</a>-<a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0003_R_d411807872e433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interface">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The reason behind this is that Na element has more abundant reserves on Earth compared with Li, and its similar storage mechanism to Li-ion based storage devices.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0004_R_d411807872e438" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nat. Rev. Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the development of SSDs necessitates higher requirements for Na-storage anodes, such as large capacity, strong stability, and high coulombic efficiency (CE).</p>
         
         <p>Carbon materials, known for their high specific surface area, chemical inertness, and good mechanical stability, are important anode materials that hold significant positions in the fields of new energy storage systems. However, their performance in storing Na is often unsatisfactory due to the larger radius of Na<sup>+</sup> compared with Li<sup>+</sup>, which would result in the slow diffusion kinetics and huge volume variation during sodiation/desodiation process, ultimately leading to the low theoretical capacity (e.g., 30 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> for NaC<sub>64</sub>) and short service life.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0005_R_d411807872e454" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Although alloying/conversion-type anode materials with enhanced capacity have been widely developed for storing Na, they still face challenges related to large volume change and unsatisfied cycling durability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0006_R_d411807872e460" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Mater.">6</a>, <a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0007_R_d411807872e460" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv. Energy. Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Anchoring alloying/conversion-type nanosized anode materials with carbons for leveraging the advantage of coupling mechanisms is currently an effective design strategy. Among various hosting carbons, including graphene,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0008_R_d411807872e465" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> nanotube,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0009_R_d411807872e471" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Carbon">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> hard carbon<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0010_R_d411807872e476" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - J. Mater. Chem. A">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and soft carbon,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0011_R_d411807872e481" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Chem. Eng. J.">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> mesoporous carbon materials with well-controlled mesoporosity offer appearance advantages. These advantages include a high specific surface area that helps disperse active nanoparticles and ready access of guest species (ions and electrolyte molecules) to active sites by decreasing diffusion lengths compared with the bulk ones.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0012_R_d411807872e487" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - J. Mater. Chem. A">12</a>, <a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0013_R_d411807872e487" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Carbon">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, current mesoporous carbon-based anodes exhibit unsatisfactory performance owing to the following reasons: 1) the fragile mesopore walls are prone to breakage during the device fabrication process, making it difficult to obtain a relatively complete conductive network; 2) the large volume change also would result into the collapse of mesoporous structure that usually cause the shedding of active substances and discontinuity in the conductive network, thereby leading to unsatisfied Na-storage performance; 3) the smaller interconnected channels between adjacent mesopore impede rapid diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>/electrolyte, making it difficult to achieve high-rate capability; 4) the extremely large surface area of mesoporous carbon can lead to excessive electrode/electrolyte interfaces that induce formation of parasitic SEI films, thereby reducing coulombic efficiency. Accordingly, designing a universal mesoporous carbon-based anode with stable electronic transport network, rapid diffusion channels of ions/electrolyte, limited surface area and weak volume variation is one of the most effective routes for achieving high-performance SSDs.</p>
         
         <p>Herein, we put forward depositing phosphorus-doped (P-doped) mesoporous carbon (PMC) onto graphene sheets of graphene aerogel (GA) to form a GA@PMC composite with 3D hierarchically porous structure. Compared with bare PMC, the GA@PMC composite used as a hosting material for active nanoparticles presents the following merits: 1) 3D cross-linked graphene sheets not only can offer conductive network to enhance the conductivity of the electrode but also can buffer the volume change of the electrode, ensuing good cycling stability; 2) interconnected macroporous structure can facilitate the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> and electrolyte; 3) the decreased surface areas can reduce the electrode/electrolyte interface, leading to upgraded coulombic efficiency (<b>Scheme</b> <a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0008">1</a>). Considering the large theoretical capacity, great reactivity and high-cost efficiency of FeSe<sub>2</sub>, FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles anchored in such GA@PMC (FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC) is taken as an example for verifying the advantages of their unique structure in storing Na<sup>+</sup>. Furthermore, the effect of FeSe<sub>2</sub> content on performance has been studied, and FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 (22.6&nbsp;wt% FeSe<sub>2</sub>) shows the best Na-storage performance, delivering a high capacity of 345.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. The optimized FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 composite was further utilized as anode in SICs, SIBs and SDIBs full-cells, employing activated carbon (AC), vanadium phosphate sodium (NVP) and expanded graphite (EG) as cathode, respectively,&nbsp;to confirm its practical application prospects. The results show that the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//AC&nbsp;SICs can reach a high energy/power density (129&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>/9411&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>) and a long cycling life (86.7% of capacitance retention at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> over 8000 cycles). The FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//NVP&nbsp;SIBs can reach a high-power density of 9866&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> at 33&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> and a good cycling stability, achieving 94.6% of capacity retention over 800 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Especially, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//EG&nbsp;SDIBs can achieve a high-power density of 15&nbsp;283&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> at 80&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>, with a long cycling life, maintaining a capacity of 138 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/43ccd2fe-3a3d-4c3e-92ec-3a71f75c9de0/adfm202406827-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/43ccd2fe-3a3d-4c3e-92ec-3a71f75c9de0/adfm202406827-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/532e45b9-4658-4236-84cd-5e8ade3f0c12/adfm202406827-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/43ccd2fe-3a3d-4c3e-92ec-3a71f75c9de0/adfm202406827-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
