      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406827-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406827-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p><b>Scheme</b> <a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0009">2</a> illustrates the schematic diagram of the preparation process of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC composite prepared by using hydrothermal reduction and templating methods. First, a mixture of GO dispersion and SiO<sub>2</sub> sol was hydrothermal reacted in a Teflon-lined autoclave, followed by vacuum freeze-drying to obtain the GA/SiO<sub>2</sub> composite. The GA/SiO<sub>2</sub> composite was subsequently immersed in an ethanol solution that contained phenolic resin and phosphoric acid. Next, the complex of GA/SiO<sub>2</sub> and carbon percussor was pre-polymerized at 100 °C and carbonized at 600 °C to produce the GA/SiO<sub>2</sub>/carbon composite. The GA@PMC composite was achieved after soaking the GA/SiO<sub>2</sub>/carbon in HF solution to remove SiO<sub>2</sub> nanospheres. The Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>/GA@PMC composite was prepared by depositing Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> nanoparticles onto PMC through high-temperature decomposition of Fe sources. Finally, FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC composite was obtained after selenizing Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> into FeSe<sub>2</sub>. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1a</a> (Supporting Information) shows an SEM image of P-doped mesoporous carbon (PMC), which presents a typical 3D ordered mesoporous structure. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0001">1a</a> unveils an SEM image of graphene aerogel (GA), exhibiting a 3D interconnected porous structure with the pore size in range of 2–10&nbsp;µm, which is similar to the reported GA in literature.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0014_R_d411807872e635" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Adv. Mater. Technol.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> After compositing with PMC, the GA@PMC well inherits typical morphology of GA, and mesoporous structure of carbon on the crumple sheet-like graphene is clearly observed (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0001">1b</a>). After FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles were deposited on GA@PMC, the mesoporous structure of carbon is still well maintained (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0001">1c</a>, SEM image of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2). The mesoporous structures of the samples were further characterized by TEM. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1b</a> (Supporting Information) exhibits a TEM image of pure PMC, showing interconnected mesopores. After loading FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles on PMC, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC composite still maintains 3D ordered mesoporous structure (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1c,d</a>, Supporting Information). When PMC is deposited on the graphene sheets of GA, although the orderliness is poor, the mesopores are still interconnected with mesopore size of ≈40&nbsp;nm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0001">1d</a>). Meanwhile, wrinkled ultrathin graphene sheets also can be identified. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0001">1e</a> shows the TEM image of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2, presenting that ultrafine nanoparticles are distributed on the mesoporous walls of carbon. The lattice fringes with a lattice spacing of 0.25&nbsp;nm in HR-TEM image (inset of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0001">1e</a>) correspond to the orthorhombic phase of FeSe<sub>2</sub>, confirming that these nanoparticles are FeSe<sub>2</sub>. The corresponding selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern and EDS elemental mapping images displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0001">1f,g</a> further verify that the FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles are successfully deposited in GA@PMC and mesoporous carbon is successfully doped with P atoms.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0009"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/5a7877aa-0a38-459b-8bc1-8a24483cd479/adfm202406827-fig-0009-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/5a7877aa-0a38-459b-8bc1-8a24483cd479/adfm202406827-fig-0009-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/19813599-8a7e-4f72-bfa8-30f47e9e28e4/adfm202406827-fig-0009-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/5a7877aa-0a38-459b-8bc1-8a24483cd479/adfm202406827-fig-0009-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Scheme 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406827-fig-0009&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406827" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Schematic illustration for the fabrication of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/3a7653ad-6c66-48af-8854-18cfb7ff2cb3/adfm202406827-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/3a7653ad-6c66-48af-8854-18cfb7ff2cb3/adfm202406827-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1ae71d6e-050e-4d81-8664-12b253655668/adfm202406827-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/3a7653ad-6c66-48af-8854-18cfb7ff2cb3/adfm202406827-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406827-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406827" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">SEM images of a) GA, b) GA@PMC, and c) FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC. TEM images of the d) GA@PMC and e) FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2. Inset of (e): the corresponding HR-TEM image of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2. f) SAED pattern of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2. g) The dark-field TEM image and the corresponding EDS elemental mappings of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The XRD patterns of the prepared composites are shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0002">2a</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2a</a> (Supporting Information). From Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0002">2a</a>, the wide XRD peak at 2θ = 24° for GA@PMC confirms the existence of SP<sup>2</sup>-carbon, which originates from rGO or partially graphitized carbon.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0015_R_d411807872e753" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Carbon">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The additional diffraction peaks for FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC are in perfect agreement with the orthorhombic phase of FeSe<sub>2</sub> (PDF#74-0247), confirming the successful deposition of FeSe<sub>2</sub> on carbon. XRD patterns of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC composites with different FeSe<sub>2</sub> content are displayed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2a</a> (Supporting Information). It can be found that the characteristic peaks for FeSe<sub>2</sub> are getting stronger, implying that more and more FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles are exposed to the GA@PMC surface as the FeSe<sub>2</sub> content increases. Their porous structures were analyzed on the basis of N<sub>2</sub> adsorption–desorption isotherms from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0002">2b</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2b</a> (Supporting Information). The FeSe<sub>2</sub>@PMC composite displays a typical IV-type curve with a H1-type loop in the relative pressure ranged from 0.80 to 0.95, demonstrating the well-ordered mesoporous structure in FeSe<sub>2</sub>@PMC. The GA@PMC and the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC composites with different FeSe<sub>2</sub> loadings all demonstrate H3-type hysteresis loops in the relative pressure of 0.45-0.9, suggesting the disordered mesoporous structure in the composites. Furthermore, compared with FeSe<sub>2</sub>@PMC, they exhibit more pronounced N<sub>2</sub> uptake at high relative pressure of 0.95–1.0, which relates to the macroporous structure caused by the stacked graphene sheets. The pore size distribution (PSD) results in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0002">2c</a> demonstrate that the introduction of FeSe<sub>2</sub> does not damage the mesoporous structure. The inset of Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2b</a> (Supporting Information) shows that FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-3 with highest FeSe<sub>2</sub> loading exhibits a sharp decrease in PSD peak at ≈30&nbsp;nm. This suggests that excessive FeSe<sub>2</sub> loading may lead to the blockage of mesopores, potentially impeding the diffusion of the electrolyte and ions. It is important to note that the pore size obtained with the PSD curve is smaller than that observed with the TEM, attributing to the deviation in the BJH model calculation, which is less suitable for cage-like pores compared with cylindrical mesopores.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0016_R_d411807872e817" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Nat. Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) data of the samples was listed in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information). Compared with FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-3, the relatively rich mesopores in FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 can provide abundant Na-ion storage sites and contribute to the rapid diffusion of electrolytes and ions. Significantly, the pore volume and specific surface area of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 are much smaller than that of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC. The introduction of GA can decrease the pore volume and surface area of the composite, which would effectively minimize the electrode/electrolyte interfaces, thereby, improving the coulombic efficiency.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0017_R_d411807872e834" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - ACS. Nano">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4548db0c-bd2e-40c3-823a-f3f66db44607/adfm202406827-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/4548db0c-bd2e-40c3-823a-f3f66db44607/adfm202406827-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/33e171cb-68bb-4609-b354-f7382c880a6e/adfm202406827-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4548db0c-bd2e-40c3-823a-f3f66db44607/adfm202406827-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406827-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406827" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns, b) N<sub>2</sub> adsorption-desorption isotherms, c) PSD curves for the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2, FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC, and GA@PMC composites. d) XPS survey spectrum of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 composite, and the corresponding high-resolution XPS spectra of e) C1s and f) P 2p.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The actual loadings of FeSe<sub>2</sub> in the composites can be determined through TGA (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3a,b</a>, Supporting Information). The small weight loss before 200 °C is caused by the evaporation of adsorbed water. The significant weight loss in the temperature range of 200–500 °C is ascribed to the carbon decomposition and the oxidation of the FeSe<sub>2</sub> to Fe<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0018_R_d411807872e881" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - J. Alloys Compd.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The FeSe<sub>2</sub> content can be calculated to be ≈20.1, 8.2, 22.6, and 41.1&nbsp;wt% for FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC, FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-1, FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-3, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0019_R_d411807872e897" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Small">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>To elucidate the chemical nature of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 composite, XPS was employed, and C1s of at 284.8&nbsp;eV was used as a reference to calibrate the XPS binding energy (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0002">2d–f</a>). As presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0002">2d</a>, the XPS survey spectrum reveals that FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 mainly consists of C, P, Se, Fe, and O elements. The C 1s spectrum shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0002">2e</a> displays the presence of various carbon bonded species including C─C (284.8&nbsp;eV), C─P, and C─O (285.6&nbsp;eV) and C═O (288.7&nbsp;eV).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0020_R_d411807872e919" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Colloids Surf. Physicochem. Eng. Aspects">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In high-resolution P 2p spectrum (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0002">2f</a>), two peaks corresponded to the P─C (133.1&nbsp;eV) and P─O (135.7&nbsp;eV) can be observed, further confirming the successfully doping of P heteroatom into mesoporous carbon.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0021_R_d411807872e927" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Adv. Energy Mater.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The XPS Se 3d core-level spectrum (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3c</a>, Supporting Information) can be divided into two peaks, which are related to Se 3d <sub>3/2</sub> at 56.1&nbsp;eV and Se 3d <sub>5/2</sub> at 55.5&nbsp;eV, assigning to the characteristic peaks in FeSe<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0022_R_d411807872e942" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Small">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Besides, the Se─Se bond (56.7&nbsp;eV) is attributed to a small amount of residual Se on the surface, and the Se─O bond (58.9&nbsp;eV) originates from the oxidation of Se in exposed air.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0023_R_d411807872e948" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Chem. Eng. J.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3d</a> (Supporting Information) shows the high-resolution Fe 2p spectrum, where the peaks at 711.1 and 724.7&nbsp;eV correspond to Fe<sup>2+</sup> in FeSe<sub>2</sub>, while the peaks at 713.5 and 726.8&nbsp;eV are indicative of Fe<sup>3+</sup> arising from the partial oxidation of Fe upon exposure to air.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0023_R_d411807872e963" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Chem. Eng. J.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the presence of Fe<sup>3+</sup> can also be confirmed by Raman detection (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>Initially, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC electrodes were optimized with respect to FeSe<sub>2</sub> contents (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information), and the resulting performance data are compiled in the radar graph (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0003">3a</a>). It has been observed that the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 with 22.6&nbsp;wt% FeSe<sub>2</sub> loading demonstrates the optimal electrochemical performance among the three electrodes in terms of rate capability, long-term cycling performance, initial coulombic efficiency (ICE), and charge transfer rate at the electrolyte/electrode interface. To further reveal the Na-storage process, CV curves of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode for the initial three cycles at 0.1&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> conducted in a potential range of 0.01–3.0&nbsp;V are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6a</a> (Supporting Information). After the first cycle, in where the solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film is formed, the reduction peaks stabilize at ≈0.7 and 1.8&nbsp;V, while the oxidation peaks become stabilize at 1.5, 1.8, 2.0, and 2.4&nbsp;V. The reduction peak is associated with the intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> into the lattice of FeSe<sub>2</sub>, forming the intermediate compound Na<sub>x</sub>FeSe<sub>2</sub>, followed by the subsequent reduction of Na<sub>x</sub>FeSe<sub>2</sub> to metallic Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>Se.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0024_R_d411807872e1017" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Commun.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The presence of multiple oxidation peaks suggests a multistep oxidation process involving the oxidation of Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>Se to form Na<sub>x</sub>FeSe<sub>2</sub>, followed by the deintercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> from Na<sub>x</sub>FeSe<sub>2</sub> to yield FeSe<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0025_R_d411807872e1037" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Rare Metals">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6b</a> (Supporting Information) shows the initial three GCD profiles of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, and the good repeatability of the GCD curve after the first cycle indicates the good reversibility of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/902e6da8-db73-4e02-a373-81ad9300dc36/adfm202406827-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/902e6da8-db73-4e02-a373-81ad9300dc36/adfm202406827-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/b794261f-13d3-4d4e-8810-8a6883014c5e/adfm202406827-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/902e6da8-db73-4e02-a373-81ad9300dc36/adfm202406827-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406827-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406827" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Radar chart for comparison of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC electrodes with different FeSe<sub>2</sub> content. b) CV curves and c) rate capabilities of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2, FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC and GA@PMC electrodes. d) Comparison of rate capability of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode and the reported anodes in the literature. e) GITT curves and ion diffusion coefficients&nbsp;of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC electrodes. f) The proportion of capacitive contribution on the total specific capacity output at different scan rate. g) Long-term cycling stabilities of the electrodes at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To clarify the important role of GA and FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles in ameliorating the Na-storage capabilities of the electrode, the electrochemical performance of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2, FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC, and GA@PMC were compared. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0003">3b</a> shows the CV curves for the electrodes at 1.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>. Compared with the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC, the stronger redox peaks for the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode suggests that GA plays a key role in accelerating the kinetics of FeSe<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0026_R_d411807872e1110" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - J. Energy Chem.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6c</a> (Supporting Information) presents the cycling performance of the electrodes at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, revealing that the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode displays better cycling stability (598.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles) than the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC (392.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and GA@PMC (212.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) electrodes. Moreover, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode shows an ICE value of 91.5%, which is higher than that of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC (83.5%) and GA@PMC (62.2%) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6d</a>, Supporting Information). Additionally, the coulombic efficiency (CE) value of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode approaches 100% after three cycles. The FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode also delivers highest capacities at each current density (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0003">3c</a>). It shows a high capacity of 543.2/311.2 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1/10 A g<sup>−1</sup> at third cycle, and its capacity can be restored to 92.4% (502.7&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup>) of the original capacity when the current density is reset to 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. On the one hand, the superior Na-storage properties of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 over those of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC highlight the important role of GA in improving the electrochemical performance; on the other hand, its better performance compared with GA@PMC also signifies the significant contribution of FeSe<sub>2</sub> active materials to Na-storage. Furthermore, the rate capabilities and cycling performance of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode can be comparable to or even better than the reported anodes in Na-ion half-cells (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0003">3d</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <p>In order to further demonstrate the advantages of mesoporous carbon in FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and the structure design of GA@PMC, FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA and pure FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles were prepared, and their performances were compared with those of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode. As displayed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information), the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA electrode demonstrates inferior electrochemical performance compare to the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode. Without the confinement effect of mesoporous carbon, the growth of FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles into larger ones leads to a diminished number of active sites. Furthermore, the absence of mesoporous carbon causes FeSe<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles to readily agglomerate and delaminate from the rGO sheets during the cycling process, compromising the cycling stability of the electrode. Similarly, without the dispersion and limitation effects of GA and PMC, the Na-storage performance of the FeSe<sub>2</sub> electrode would also be poor (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information). These findings underscore the critical importance of electrode architecture design in enhancing their electrochemical performance.</p>
         
         <p>In order to further reveal the effect of the GA on promoting the diffusion of Na-ion in the electrode and on enhancing the electronic conductivity, the galvanostatic intermittent titration (GITT) and EIS measurements were carried out. As can be observed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0003">3e</a>, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode harvests higher Na-ion diffusion coefficient (<span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/a751cb3f-b327-4cbd-8745-ebabd51d69d1/adfm202406827-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202406827:adfm202406827-math-0001" display="inline" location="graphic/adfm202406827-math-0001.png">
               <semantics>
                  <msub>
                     <mi>D</mi>
                     <mrow>
                        <mi mathvariant="normal">N</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${{D}_{{\mathrm{N}}{{{\mathrm{a}}}^{\mathrm{ + }}}}}$</annotation>
               </semantics></math>) values compared with FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC electrode, confirming the key role of GA in accelerating the diffusion kinetics of Na-ion in the electrode. The EIS results in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information) reveal that the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode has a smaller charge transfer resistance (R<sub>ct</sub>) value (10.42 Ω) compared with FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC (15.88 Ω), indicating that the GA can accelerate the charge transfer at electrolyte/electrode interfaces of the electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0026_R_d411807872e1235" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - J. Energy Chem.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">The reaction kinetics analysis of the composites was further conducted to understand the great Na-storage performance of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode by employing CV measurements carried out at scan rates of 0.2–1.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a>, Supporting Information). As displayed in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10a</a> (Supporting Information), along with the increase of the scan rate, the position of redox peaks for the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode maintains almost univariable, which suggests low polarization and fast reaction kinetics of the electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0027_R_d411807872e1256" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, compared with the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC electrode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10b</a>, Supporting Information), the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode shows much stronger redox peaks at each scan rate, verifying its superior Na-storage activity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0026_R_d411807872e1269" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - J. Energy Chem.">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The charge storage mechanism was analyzed by plotting the relationship between scan rate (<i>v</i>) and peak current density (<i>i</i>) based on the formula below:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0028_R_d411807872e1278" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Energy Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202406827-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/e390004c-9a48-4c99-bf65-f7b11b11a535/adfm202406827-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202406827:adfm202406827-math-0002" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202406827-math-0002.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>i</mi>
                           <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                           <mrow>
                              <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                              <mspace width="0.33em"></mspace>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                           </mrow>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>v</mi>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">b</mi>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}i\ {\mathrm{ = \ a}}{{v}^{\mathrm{b}}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(1)</span></div>where a and b are the adjustable parameters. More specifically, b-value of 0.5 indicates the diffusion-controlled behavior resulting from slowly semi-infinite linear ion diffusion; b-value of 1.0 implies the capacitive behavior, which is associated with the rapid Faradaic reactions occurring at the electrolyte/FeSe<sub>2</sub> interface. According to Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10c,d</a> (Supporting Information), the b values of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode are measured at 0.96/0.93 for cathodic/anodic process, which is larger than that of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC electrode (0.96/0.82). It is proved that the GA plays a major role in improving capacitive contribution ratios. The concrete proportion of capacitive contribution can be calculated by the following equation:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0029_R_d411807872e1313" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>
            
            <div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202406827-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/b7cbf697-5d5c-427e-8873-f8a1998ddd37/adfm202406827-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:1616301X:media:adfm202406827:adfm202406827-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/adfm202406827-math-0003.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>i</mi>
                           <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">V</mi>
                           </mfenced>
                           <mspace width="2.79999pt"></mspace>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>k</mi>
                              <mn mathvariant="italic">1</mn>
                           </msub>
                           <mspace width="2.79999pt"></mspace>
                           <mi>v</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>k</mi>
                              <mn>2</mn>
                           </msub>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>v</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mn>1</mn>
                                 <mo>/</mo>
                                 <mn>2</mn>
                              </mrow>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation} i\left(\mathrm{V}\right)\hspace*{0.28em}={k}_{\mathit{1}}\hspace*{0.28em}v+{k}_{2}{v}^{1/2} \end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>where <i>i</i>(V) corresponds to the current density at a certain voltage, k<sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and k<sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> represent the surface-induced capacitive and diffusive contribution. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0003">3f</a> illustrates the capacitive contribution ratios of the electrodes. Compared with the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC electrode, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode achieves a higher capacitive contribution ratio at each scan rate, indicating that it possesses faster reaction kinetics. Furthermore, in pace with the climb of scan rate, the capacitive contribution ratio rises, reaching up to 91.4% and 77.8% for the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC electrodes at 1.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11 and S12</a>, Supporting Information). The high proportion of capacitance contribution at high scan rates contributes to good high-rate capability. Long-term cycling performances of the electrodes at a high current density of 5 A g<sup>−1</sup> are depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0003">3g</a>, where the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode delivers a larger capacity after 1000 cycles (345.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) compared with the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/PMC electrode (117.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). After the cycling process, the mesoporous carbon deposited on the rGO sheets remains clearly visible (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information), further indicating the structural stability of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode. Moreover, in order to validate the versatility and universality of our strategy, MoS<sub>2</sub> nanoparticles were deposited on GA@PMC to prepare MoS<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC composite (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information). When employed as anode, the MoS<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC electrode displays superior electrochemical properties.</div>
         
         <p>The Na-storage mechanism of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode can be further characterized by ex situ XRD analysis. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0004">4a</a> illustrates the GCD curve for the first cycle of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode and 9 distinct discharge/charge states are marked. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0004">4b</a> shows the XRD spectra of the electrodes selected at these 9 states. The FeSe<sub>2</sub> peak located at 2θ = 31.2°, 34.9°, 36.3°, 44.8°, and 48.4° at OCV state gradually disappear with the discharge process, meanwhile, new diffraction peaks of Na<sub>2</sub>Se appear. With the process of recharging, peaks for Na<sub>2</sub>Se disappear and peaks for FeSe<sub>2</sub> reappear.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0030_R_d411807872e1433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Chem. Eng. J.">30</a>, <a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0031_R_d411807872e1433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0004">4c</a> is the corresponding 2D contour plot of the XRD, indicating the conversion of FeSe<sub>2</sub> into Na<sub>2</sub>Se during the discharging process and the reverse conversion of Na<sub>2</sub>Se into FeSe<sub>2</sub> during the charging process. This phenomenon demonstrates the reversibility of FeSe<sub>2</sub>, which also can be confirmed by the ex situ Raman analysis (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information) and the following HR-TEM analysis. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0004">4d</a> shows the HR-TEM images of the electrodes at state 5 (discharged to 0.1&nbsp;V) and state 9 (recharged to 3&nbsp;V), revealing lattice stripes with a mean lattice spacing of 0.21 and 0.25&nbsp;nm, assigning to (311) plane of Na<sub>2</sub>Se and (120) plane of FeSe<sub>2</sub>, respectively.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/47b2c79f-951f-4958-974c-ec1c206b5023/adfm202406827-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/47b2c79f-951f-4958-974c-ec1c206b5023/adfm202406827-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/5ec8fe7a-dae3-4eac-86c4-448f28f646fe/adfm202406827-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/47b2c79f-951f-4958-974c-ec1c206b5023/adfm202406827-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406827-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406827" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The GCD curve of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. b) Ex situ XRD patterns and c) the corresponding contour plot of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode. d) HR-TEM images of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode selected at the state 5 and state 9. The optimized structure and the corresponding electron density differences of e) Na-ion adsorbed on FeSe<sub>2</sub> surface and FeSe<sub>2</sub>/C interface and f) Na<sub>2</sub>Se adsorbed on pure carbon and P-doped carbon structures. The yellow, green, orange, black, and purple balls indicate Na, Se, Fe, C, and P atoms and the red and blue areas denote electron accumulation and depletion.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To deepen the understanding of good electrochemical performance of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode, density functional theory (DFT) calculation was employed for obtaining the adsorption energies of Na atoms on bulk FeSe<sub>2</sub> and FeSe<sub>2</sub>-carbon composite structure (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0004">4e</a>). As can be calculated, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/C composite has a higher Na adsorption energy than bulk FeSe<sub>2</sub> structure, indicating more Na atoms can be adsorbed into the composite, thereby enhancing the capacity of the composite electrode. Meanwhile, in order to confirm the beneficial effect of doped P on the performance of the electrode, the adsorption of discharge products (Na<sub>2</sub>Se) on both pure carbon and P-C sites were simulated. As illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0004">4f</a>, the adsorption energy of Na<sub>2</sub>Se on P-doped carbon is −0.88&nbsp;eV, much lower than that on pure carbon (−0.47&nbsp;eV), demonstrating that the doped P can enhance the adsorption of the discharge products, and thus, improving the stability of the electrode.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0032_R_d411807872e1522" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Carbon">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>In order to evaluate the practical application of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2, FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//AC SICs were assembled by employing FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 as anode and AC as cathode. As illustrated in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0005">5a</a>, during discharging, Na<sup>+</sup> cations are deintercalated out of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 anode and PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> anions are desorbed from the surface of AC cathode; the charging process is exactly the opposite. In order to balance the charge between the anode and cathode, the mass ratio between FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and AC was determined to be 1:2 by assessing the electrochemical performance of SICs with different mass ratio of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 to AC (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16a–c</a>, Supporting Information). The operating voltage window was set at 0.5–4&nbsp;V (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16d</a>, Supporting Information). At this voltage range, the SICs exhibit a GCD curve with a quasi-triangular shape, demonstrating a better symmetry compared with anode, which would provide higher power densities (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0005">5b</a>). GCD curves of SICs at different current density are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0005">5c</a>, and almost no deformation of the curves implies the good reversible of SICs. After calculation, the energy density of this SICs can reach 129&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 190&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> based on the total mass of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and AC, and it still maintains at 40&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> even at a high-power density of 9411&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0005">5d</a>). Furthermore, the SICs demonstrate superior electrochemical performance compare to the reported SICs such as MoO<sub>2</sub>//MoSe<sub>2</sub>/G//AC,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0033_R_d411807872e1585" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - J. Power Sources">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> FeS<sub>2-x</sub>Se<sub>x</sub>//AC,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0034_R_d411807872e1594" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interface">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Fe<sub>8</sub>Se<sub>7</sub>@NC//AC,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0035_R_d411807872e1604" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Colloid Interface Sci.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> E-ReSe<sub>2</sub>@INC//AC,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0036_R_d411807872e1612" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Cu<sub>1.8</sub>Se/C//AC,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0037_R_d411807872e1619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Sustainable Mater. Techno.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and CoSeO<sub>3</sub>//AC<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0038_R_d411807872e1627" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Chem. Eng. J.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0005">5d</a>). In addition, the cycling stability of the SICs shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0005">5e</a> reveals a capacitance retention of 86.7% after 8000 cycles, suggesting a good cycling stability of our SICs.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/768926d6-0a4c-47c6-86ab-3f55f35ad2d6/adfm202406827-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/768926d6-0a4c-47c6-86ab-3f55f35ad2d6/adfm202406827-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/685203f7-5b30-4112-96ef-039b4900389e/adfm202406827-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/768926d6-0a4c-47c6-86ab-3f55f35ad2d6/adfm202406827-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406827-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406827" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic illustration of discharge process of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//AC SICs. b) The selected operating potential range of the anode, cathode, and SICs. c) GCD curves of the SICs. d) Comparison between Ragone plots of our SICs and the reported SICs. e) Long-term cycling performance of SICs at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. f) Comparison between Ragone plots of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//NVP SIBs and the results in the literature; g) Long-term cycling performance of our SIBs at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode was also applied as anode in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) full-cells with NVP cathode to further evaluate its potential application. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17a,b</a> (Supporting Information) shows GCD curves and rate capability of NVP cathode in Na-ion half-cells. The mass ratio of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 to NVP is fixed at 1:3 by evaluating the properties of the SIBs with different mass ratio of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 to NVP (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17c,d</a>, Supporting Information). In Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17e</a> (Supporting Information), the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//NVP SIBs with the mass ratio of 1:3 can maintain the capacity at 113.1, 92.6, 67.7, 51.4, 37.7, and 22.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> when the current density ranging from 0.1 to 5 A g<sup>−1</sup> (based on the mass of NVP). Accordingly, the SIBs exhibit a large energy density of 164&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at 195&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> and deliver an energy density of 33&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> when the power density climbs to 9866&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> based on the total mass of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and NVP, which is superior to the reported SIBs full-cells such as TiO<sub>2</sub>//NVP,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0039_R_d411807872e1704" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Nano-Micro Lett.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> FeP@OCF//NVP,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0040_R_d411807872e1710" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> NaTi(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>//NVP,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0041_R_d411807872e1719" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> WSSe@CPCS//NVPF<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0042_R_d411807872e1725" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Small">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and SnP<sub>2</sub>O<sub>7</sub>/rGO//NVP/C<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0043_R_d411807872e1734" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0005">5f</a>). Furthermore, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//NVP SIBs deliver a high capacity of 85.8&nbsp;mA h g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17f</a>, Supporting Information), and a capacity of 60.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> can be maintained after 800 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to a 94.6% capacity retention rate of initial capacity (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0005">5g</a>).</p>
         
         <p>Given the great stability and rapid reaction kinetics of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 anode, Na-ion based dual-ion batteries (SDIBs) are constructed using expanded graphite (EG) as cathode. The schematic illustration in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0006">6a</a> depicts the discharge/charge mechanism the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//EG SDIBs: during charging procedure, PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> anions are intercalated into the layers of EG, while Na<sup>+</sup> cations are intercalated into the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode; during discharging procedure, PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> are deintercalated from EG cathode and FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 anode, respectively, and return to the electrolyte.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0044_R_d411807872e1790" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - Small">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> CV curves of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//Na and EG//Na half-cells are presented in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0006">6b</a>. These curves indicate that the intercalation/deintercalation of Na-ion in anode occurs at a low working potential (0.01–3.0&nbsp;V), while the insertion/extraction of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> anions in cathode takes place at a high working potential (3.0–5.0&nbsp;V). Consequently, this results in a high working voltage for SDIBs. The voltage range of the SDIBs full-cells is set to be 1.5–5&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0006">6c</a>), whereby undesirable side reactions such as electrolyte decomposition can be avoided.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0045_R_d411807872e1807" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Nat. Commun.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, to ensure the charge balance between anode and cathode, the cycling stability and rate performance of SDIBs full-cells with various mass ratio of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 to EG were measured. The cycling performance in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0006">6d</a> shows that the assembled SDIBs with a mass ratio of 1:3 can maintain a specific capacity of 188 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, which is higher than that of the SDIBs with mass ratios of 1:2 (141 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and 1:4 (122 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>). Also, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//EG SDIBs with a mass ratio of 1:3 demonstrate the best rate capability, delivering the discharge capacities of 231.4, 202.7, 187.6, 179.4, 159.8, 133.0, and 105.6 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2, 0.3, 0.5, 0.8, 1.0, 2.0, and 5.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (based on the mass of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0006">6e</a>). Thus, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 to EG mass ratio is controlled as 1: 3 for the following tests. The GCD plots at different rate are displayed in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0006">6f</a>. The GCD curves exhibit a consistent shape without excessive increase in discharge/charge voltage separation, suggesting the low electrochemical polarization of the SDIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0046_R_d411807872e1843" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - Nano-Micro Lett.">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> From Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0006">6g</a>, our SDIBs achieve an energy density of up to 232&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>at 775&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the total mass of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 and EG), and they can maintain a high energy density of 80&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> even at a high-power density of 15&nbsp;283&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>. Also, the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//EG SDIBs lies in a leading position as observed from the comparison of the Ragone plot of this SDIBs with the other reported SDIBs, including WSSe@CPCS//EG,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0042_R_d411807872e1865" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Small">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> MoSSe-NSs@NC//EG,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0047_R_d411807872e1870" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> NbSSe/NC//EG,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0048_R_d411807872e1876" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Nano-Micro Lett.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> MoS<sub>1.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>@C//EG,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0045_R_d411807872e1885" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Nat. Commun.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and P-HCNS//EG.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0049_R_d411807872e1891" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - J. Mater. Chem. A">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the SDIBs deliver a high capacity of 138.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention of 86.4% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0006">6h</a>) and can continuously light up the Fe-shaped Logo for &gt;2 min. These results confirm that the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//EG SDIBs shows excellent cyclic stability and certain practical application prospects.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/89d376b6-ec57-499a-adcb-9c410c0e21fc/adfm202406827-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/89d376b6-ec57-499a-adcb-9c410c0e21fc/adfm202406827-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4fc8233f-7ad3-4eaf-9098-2fef887be0f5/adfm202406827-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/89d376b6-ec57-499a-adcb-9c410c0e21fc/adfm202406827-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406827-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406827" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//EG full-cells: a) Schematic illustration of the SDIBs; b) CV curve of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//Na and EG//Na half-cells; c) GCD curves of half-cells and full-cells; d) Cycling performances and e) rate capabilities of SDIBs with different mass ratio of FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 to EG at 0.5 A g<sup>−1</sup>; f) GCD curves of SDIBs at different rate. g) The Ragone plots of SDIBs compared with results in literature; h) Cycling stability of the SDIBs at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In order to explore the charge storage mechanism of the EG cathode, ex situ XRD analysis was carried out. <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0007">7a</a> presents the GCD curve of the EG//Na half-cells for the first cycle, with the selected discharge/charge states labeled on the curve. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0007">7b,c</a> shows the XRD data of the EG electrode at different states, along with the corresponding 2D contour plot&nbsp;in the&nbsp;range&nbsp;of&nbsp;2θ = 10–40°. As can be observed, when the voltage rises to 4&nbsp;V, the typical graphene (002) peak at 26.3° vanishes while two diffraction peaks at 25.1° and 29.6° emerge. With a further increase in voltage, these two peaks shift to the lower and higher angles, respectively. This phenomenon is attributed to the intercalation of anions into the layers of EG, which leads to an increased interlayer spacing of some graphite layers while compressing others (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0007">7d</a>). During the discharge process, these two peaks begin to shift back and eventually merge into one peak, corresponding to the deintercalation of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> anoions from EG. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202406827-fig-0007">7e,f</a> displays an enlarged XRD pattern and the corresponding 2D contour plot within a 2θ range of 40°–60°. Similarly, at state 6, the typical graphene (004) peak at 54.5° disappears, and two new diffraction peaks at 51.4° and 56.3° attributed to (00n+1) and (00n+2) planes appear and migrate toward the lower and higher angles, respectively, suggesting continuous intercalation of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> into EC layers. During the discharge process, the two peaks gradually merge into one peak, indicating that the PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> ions have deintercalated from the EG layer again. These results demonstrate the good reversibility of the intercalation/deintercalation of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> anions into/from EG.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0047_R_d411807872e1967" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">47</a>, <a href="#adfm202406827-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202406827-bib-0050_R_d411807872e1967" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Adv. Energy. Mater.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202406827-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f70d3b73-b2fa-42fb-87a0-2f2cc160ffe5/adfm202406827-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f70d3b73-b2fa-42fb-87a0-2f2cc160ffe5/adfm202406827-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/93ca5217-2d10-4dd6-86dd-d5993e37e486/adfm202406827-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f70d3b73-b2fa-42fb-87a0-2f2cc160ffe5/adfm202406827-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202406827-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202406827" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) GCD curve of the EG//Na half-cells at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup> for the first cycle. b,c) Ex situ XRD patterns of the EG electrode and the corresponding 2D contour plot. d) Schematic illustration of the intercalation/deintercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> into/from EG. e,f) The enlarged ex situ XRD patterns and the corresponding 2D contour plot.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202406827-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202406827-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>To conclude, a versatile phosphorus-doped mesoporous carbon (PMC) armed by graphene aerogel (GA) (GA@PMC) has been developed for hosting Na-storage active nanoparticles. Also, exemplified by FeSe<sub>2</sub>, the application of the FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC composite for Na-ion based storage devices (SSDs) have been accomplished. The optimized FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2 electrode can achieve a high specific capacity of 345.1 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles in Na-ion half-cells. The as-prepared FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//AC SICs exhibit a large maximum energy/power density of 129&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>/9411&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> with a long service life (86.7% of capacitance retention over 8000 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>). Moreover, the assembled FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//NVP SIBs also can reach a superior energy/power density of 164&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>/9866&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup> and a great stability (94.6% of the initial capacity after 800 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>). In addition, the as-constructed FeSe<sub>2</sub>/GA@PMC-2//EG SDIBs show exceptional maximum energy/power density of 234&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>/15&nbsp;283&nbsp;W kg<sup>−1</sup>, along with superior cycling stability, maintaining 86.4% of the initial capacity after 1000 cycles at 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. This remarkable performance is primarily attributed to the synergistic effect of each component within the composite. The interconnected graphene sheets can not only provide a conductive network to enhance the conductivity and kinetic response of the electrode, but also buffer the volume expansion of the active material for good cycling stability. The interconnected macropores in GA can provide rapid diffusion channels for ions/electrolyte. Furthermore, the introduction of GA can reduce the specific surface area, which consequently diminishes the electrode/electrolyte interface, leading to improved coulombic efficiency. Additionally, the DFT calculations indicate that the doping P in carbon can enhance the adsorption of discharge product (Na<sub>2</sub>Se) on carbon, which can enhance the stability of the electrode. Overall, given its ease of synthesis, cost-efficiency, and superior electrochemical performance, we anticipate that the GA@PMC-based electrode will find promising applications in a wide range of electrochemical energy storage systems.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

                  <li data-bib-id="adfm202406827-bib-0001"><span class="bullet">1</span><span class="author">J. Song</span>, <span class="author">B. Xiao</span>, <span class="author">Y.
